jQuery * Selector



Example

Select all elements inside the document:

$("*")


Open in separate window
View full source code

<html>
<head>
<script 
src="https://ajax.googleapis.com/ajax/libs/jquery/3.5.1/jquery.min.js">
</script><!--   w  w w .  d   e m  o  2  s    .c   o m  -->
<script>
$(document).ready(function(){
  $("*").css("background-color", "yellow");
});
</script>
</head>
<body>

<h1>Welcome to My Homepage</h1>

<p class="intro">My name is Javascript.</p>
<p>I live in client side.</p>
<p>My best friend is Browser.</p>

<p>Who is your favourite:</p>

<ul id="choose">
  <li>Javascript</li>
  <li>HTML</li>
  <li>CSS</li>
</ul>

</body>
</html>



Description

The * selector selects all elements in the document, including html, head and body.

If the * selector is used together with another element, it selects all child elements within the specified element.


Syntax


$("*")

Example, select all element under body elements.

$("body *").css("background-color", "yellow");


Open in separate window
View full source code

<head>
<script 
src="https://ajax.googleapis.com/ajax/libs/jquery/3.5.1/jquery.min.js">
</script><!--   w  w w  .  d e  m    o  2  s . c   o   m-->
<script>
$(document).ready(function(){
  $("body *").css("background-color", "yellow");
});
</script>
</head>
<body>

<h1>Welcome to My Homepage</h1>

<p class="intro">My name is Javascript.</p>
<p>I live in client side.</p>
<p>My best friend is Browser.</p>

</body>

jQuery :animated Selector



Example

Select any element that is currently animated:

$(":animated")


Open in separate window
View full source code

<html>
<head>
<script 
src="https://ajax.googleapis.com/ajax/libs/jquery/3.5.1/jquery.min.js">
</script><!-- w  w  w  .  d    e m   o2  s   .   co    m-->
<script>
$(document).ready(function(){
  function aniDiv(){
    $("div:eq(0)").animate({width: "50%"}, "slow");
    $("div:eq(0)").animate({width: "100%"}, "slow", aniDiv);
  }
  aniDiv();
  $(".btn1").click(function(){
    $(":animated").css("background-color", "red");
  });
});
</script>
</head>
<body>

<button class="btn1">Change color of the animated element</button>

<div style="background:blue;">Div 1</div>
<div style="background:green;">Div 2</div>
<div style="background:yellow;">Div 3</div>

</body>
</html>



Description

The :animated selector selects all elements that are currently animated.


Syntax


$(":animated")


jQuery [attribute^=value] Selector



Example

Select all <input> elements with a name attribute that starts with "lang":

$("input[name^='lang']")


Open in separate window
View full source code

<html>
<head>
<script 
src="https://ajax.googleapis.com/ajax/libs/jquery/3.5.1/jquery.min.js">
</script><!-- w    w w .    d e m  o   2  s  .   c  o  m-->
<script>
$(document).ready(function(){
  $("input[name^='lang']").css("background-color", "yellow");});
</script>
</head>
<body>

<input name="language" type="text" value="Chinese">
<input name="lang" type="text" value="English">
<input name="country" type="text" value="Germany">
<input name="anotherlanguage" type="text" value="CSS">

<p>This selector selects all input fields with the attribute name that 
starts with 'lang'.</p>

</body>
</html>



Description

The [attribute^=value] selector selects each element with a specific attribute, 
with a value beginning in a specific string.


Syntax


$("[attribute^='value']")




Parameter   Description



attribute   Required.                 
   Sets the attribute to find


value   Required.                                  
   Sets the string the value should begin with

Description

The [attribute*=value] selector selects each element with a specific attribute, 
with a value containing a string.


Syntax


$("[attribute*='value']")




Parameter   Description



attribute   Required.                 
   Sets the attribute to find


value   Required.            
   Sets the string value





jQuery [attribute~=value] Selector



Example

Select all <input> elements with a name attribute 
that contains the specific word "lang":

This selector selects all input fields with the attribute name that 
contains the specific string 'lang'.

It will only select the attribute name that 
contains the specific string "lang", and not the attribute 
name that starts, includes or ends with "lang", such as like language, 
xlangx or anotherlanguage.

$("input[name~='lang']")


Open in separate window
View full source code

<html>
<head>
<script 
src="https://ajax.googleapis.com/ajax/libs/jquery/3.5.1/jquery.min.js">
</script><!--   w  w  w  . d e  m   o   2s  .   c  o   m-->
<script>
$(document).ready(function(){
  $("input[name~='lang']").css("background-color", "yellow");});
</script>
</head>
<body>

<input name="language" type="text" value="Chinese">
<input name="lang" type="text" value="English">
<input name="country" type="text" value="Germany">
<input name="anotherlanguage" type="text" value="CSS">

</body>
</html>



Description

The [attribute~=value] selector selects each element with a specific attribute, with a value containing a specific string.

The string can contain whitespace.


Syntax


$("[attribute~='value']")




Parameter   Description



attribute   Required.                 
   Sets the attribute to find


value   Required.            
   Sets the string value

Description

The [attribute!=value] selector selects each element that does NOT have the specified attribute and value.

Elements with the selected attribute, but with a different value, will be selected.


Syntax


$("[attribute!='value']")




Parameter   Description



attribute   Required.                 
   Sets the attribute to find


value   Required.             
   Sets the value to find





jQuery [attribute|=value] Selector



Example

Select all <p> elements with a title attribute that starts with the value "Tomorrow":

$("p[title|='Tomorrow']")


Open in separate window
View full source code

<html>
<head>
<script 
src="https://ajax.googleapis.com/ajax/libs/jquery/3.5.1/jquery.min.js">
</script><!-- w   w  w .    de  m    o 2 s  .  c  o  m  -->
<script>
$(document).ready(function(){
  $("p[title|='Tomorrow']").css("background-color", "yellow");});
</script>
</head>
<body>

<p title="Tomorrow">This is a paragraph.</p>
<p title="tomorrow">This is a paragraph.</p>
<p title="Tom">This is a paragraph.</p>
<p title="See You Tomorrow">This is a paragraph.</p>
<p title="Tomorrow-the day after today">This is a paragraph.</p>

<p>This selector selects all elements with a title 
attribute value equal to 'Tomorrow', or starting with 'Tomorrow' 
followed by a hyphen.</p>

</body>
</html>



Description

The [attribute|=value] selector selects each element with a specified attribute, with a value equal to a specified string (like "en") or starting with that string followed by a hyphen (like "en-us").

This selector is often used to handle language attributes.


Syntax


$("[attribute|='value']")




Parameter   Description



attribute   Required.                 
   Sets the attribute to find


value   Required.                                            
   Sets the string the attribute value should start with




More Examples


$("a[hreflang|='en']").css("background-color", "yellow");


Open in separate window
View full source code

<html>
<head>
<script 
src="https://ajax.googleapis.com/ajax/libs/jquery/3.5.1/jquery.min.js">
</script><!-- w   w  w  .  d e    m o  2  s .  c   o m  -->
<script>
$(document).ready(function(){
  $("a[hreflang|='en']").css("background-color", "yellow");});
</script>
</head>
<body>

<a href="https://demo2s.com" hreflang="en">demo2s.com</a><br>
<a href="https://demo2s.com" hreflang="en-us">demo2s.com</a><br>
<a href="https://demo2s.com" hreflang="us-en">demo2s.com</a><br>
<a href="https://demo2s.com" hreflang="fr">demo2s.com</a>

<p>This selector selects both "en" and "en-us".</p>

</body>
</html>

Description

The .class selector selects all elements with the specific class.

The class refers to the class attribute of an HTML element.

The class attribute is used to set a particular style for several HTML elements.

Do not start a class attribute with a number. It may cause problems in some browsers.


Syntax


$(".class")




Parameter   Description


class   Required.                               
   Sets the class of the elements to select


Example


$("p.intro").css("background-color", "yellow");

  $("p.intro").css("background-color", "yellow");
});
</script>

</script><!--   w w   w  .d    e  mo  2  s   . c  o    m-->
<script>
$(document).ready(function(){
  $("p:contains(is)").css("background-color", "yellow");
});
</script>
</head>
<body>

<h1>Welcome to My Homepage</h1>

<p class="intro">My name is Javascript.</p>
<p>I live in client side.</p>
<p>My best friend is Browser.</p>

Who is your favourite:
<ul id="choose">
  <li>Javascript</li>
  <li>HTML</li>
  <li>CSS</li>
</ul>

</body>
</html>



Description

The :contains() selector selects elements containing the specified string.

The string can be contained directly in the element as text, or in a child element.

This is often used with another selector to select the elements containing the text in a group.

The text is case sensitive.


Syntax


$(":contains(text)")




Parameter   Description


text   Required.            
   Sets the text to find

Description

The :eq() selector selects an element with a specific index number.

The index numbers start at 0, and the first element has the index number 0.

This is often used with another selector to select a specifically indexed element in a group.


Syntax

Parameter   Description


index   Required.                     
    Sets the index of the element

Description

The :even selector selects each element with an even index number (like: 0, 2, 4, etc.).

The index numbers start at 0.

This selector is often used with another selector to select every even indexed element in a group.

You can use the :odd selector to select elements with odd index numbers.


Syntax


$(":even")


jQuery :first Selector



Example

Select the first <p> element:

$("p:first")


Open in separate window
View full source code

src="https://ajax.googleapis.com/ajax/libs/jquery/3.5.1/jquery.min.js">

<p>This is the second paragraph.</p>
<p>This is the last paragraph.</p>

</body>
</html>



Description

The :first selector selects the first element.

This selector can only select one single element. 

You can use the :first-child selector to select the first child for each parent element.

This is mostly used together with another selector to select the first element in a group.

To select the last element in a group, you can use the :last selector.


Syntax


$(":first")


Example


$(document).ready(function(){
  $("#btn1").click(function(){
    $("p:first").css("background-color", "red");
  });
  $("#btn2").click(function(){
    $("p:first-child").css("background-color", "yellow");
  });
});


Open in separate window
View full source code

<html>
<head>
<script 
src="https://ajax.googleapis.com/ajax/libs/jquery/3.5.1/jquery.min.js">
</script><!-- w  w   w  .  d  e  m  o 2    s  .c   o   m-->
<script>
$(document).ready(function(){
  $("#btn1").click(function(){
    $("p:first").css("background-color", "red");
  });
  $("#btn2").click(function(){
    $("p:first-child").css("background-color", "yellow");
  });
});
</script>
</head>
<body>

<button id="btn1">:first</button>
<button id="btn2">:first-child</button><br><br>

<div style="border:1px solid">
  <p>The first paragraph in div.</p>
  <p>The last paragraph in the div.</p>
</div><br>

<div style="border:1px solid">
  <p>The first paragraph in another div.</p>
  <p>The last paragraph in another div.</p>
</div>

</body>
</html>

You can use the :last-child selector to select elements that are the last child of their parent.

$(document).ready(function(){
  $("#btn1").click(function(){
    $("p:first").css("background-color", "red");
  });
  $("#btn2").click(function(){
    $("p:first-child").css("background-color", "yellow");
  });
});

$(document).ready(function(){
  $("button").click(function(){
    let btn = $(this).text();
    $("p").css("background-color", "white");
    $("p" + btn).css("background-color", "yellow");
  });
});


Open in separate window
View full source code

<html>
<head>
<script 
src="https://ajax.googleapis.com/ajax/libs/jquery/3.5.1/jquery.min.js">
</script><!--   ww  w    .d   e  m   o 2  s .    c o  m -->
<script>
$(document).ready(function(){
  $("button").click(function(){
    let btn = $(this).text();
    $("p").css("background-color", "white");
    $("p" + btn).css("background-color", "yellow");
  });
});
</script>
</head>
<body>

<p>The first paragraph in body, and the first child in div.</p>

<div style="border:1px solid;">
  <p>The first paragraph in div, and the first child in div.</p>
  <p>The last paragraph in div, and the last child in div.</p>
</div><br>

  <span>This is a span element, and the first child in this div.</span>
  <p>The first paragraph in another div, and the second child in this div.</p>
  <p>The last paragraph in another div, and the third child in this div.</p>
  <span>This is a span element, and the last child in this div.</span>
</div><br>

<div style="border:1px solid">
  <p>The first paragraph in another div, and the first child in this div.</p>
  <p>The last paragraph in the another div, and the last child in this div.</p>
</div>

<p>The last paragraph in body, and the last child in div.</p>

<button>:first-of-type</button><br><br>

The :first-of-type selector selects all elements that are the first child, of a particular type, of their parent.

This is the same as :nth-of-type(1).

You can use the :last-of-type selector to select all elements that are the last child, of a particular type, of their parent.


Syntax


$(":first-of-type")

Data Structure custom array



Javascript Source Code

The Javascript source code to do "Javascript Data Structure custom array" is

function MyArray() {
    var arg = arguments;
    this.toString = function () {
        var string = arg[0];
        for (var i = 1; i < arg.length; i++) {
            string += "," + arg[i];
        }/*w  w  w  .  d   e m   o   2s   .  c o   m */
        return string;
    }
    this.length = arg.length;
    this.push = function() {
        for (var i = 0; i < arguments.length; i++) {
            arg[arg.length++] = arguments[i];
        }
        return arg.length;
    }
    this.pop = function() {
        return arg[--arg.length];
    }
    this.join = function (j) {
        var strJoin = arg[0];
        for (var i = 1; i < arg.length; i++) {
            strJoin += j + arg[i];
        }
        return strJoin;
    }
}
var a = new MyArray(1, 2, 3, "test");
console.log(a.toString()); // 1,2,3,test
console.log(a.length); // 4
console.log(a.push('boo'));
console.log(a.toString());
console.log(a.pop());
console.log(a.join(','));
console.log(a.join(' isn\'t '));

        for (var i = 1; i < arg.length; i++) {
            string += "," + arg[i];
        }
        return string;
    }

        for (var i = 0; i < arguments.length; i++) {
            arg[arg.length++] = arguments[i];
        }
        return arg.length;
    }

        return arg[--arg.length];
    }
    this.join = function (j) {
        var strJoin = arg[0];
        for (var i = 1; i < arg.length; i++) {
            strJoin += j + arg[i];
        }
        return strJoin;
    }
}
